     1	use bytes::Bytes;
     2	use serde::Serialize;
     3	use std::ops::Bound::{Excluded, Included, Unbounded};
     4	use std::ops::{Bound, RangeBounds};
     5	
     6	use crate::comparable_range::{ComparableRange, EndBound, StartBound};
     7	
     8	/// Concrete struct representing a range of Bytes. Gets around much of
     9	/// the cumbersome work associated with the generic trait RangeBounds<Bytes>
    10	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq, Ord, PartialOrd, Hash)]
    11	pub(crate) struct BytesRange {
    12	    inner: ComparableRange<Bytes>,
    13	}
    14	
    15	impl Serialize for BytesRange {
    16	    fn serialize<S>(&self, serializer: S) -> Result<S::Ok, S::Error>
    17	    where
    18	        S: serde::Serializer,
    19	    {
    20	        self.inner.serialize(serializer)
    21	    }
    22	}
    23	
    24	#[cfg(test)]
    25	// Checks for the annoying case when we have ("prefix", "prefix\0").
    26	// When both bounds are excluded, the range is empty even though
    27	// "prefix" < "prefix\0".
    28	pub(crate) fn is_prefix_increment(prefix: &[u8], b: &[u8]) -> bool {
    29	    if !b.starts_with(prefix.as_ref()) {
    30	        return false;
    31	    }
    32	
    33	    b[prefix.len()..] == [u8::MIN]
    34	}
    35	
    36	impl RangeBounds<Bytes> for BytesRange {
    37	    fn start_bound(&self) -> Bound<&Bytes> {
    38	        self.inner.start_bound()
    39	    }
    40	
    41	    fn end_bound(&self) -> Bound<&Bytes> {
    42	        self.inner.end_bound()
    43	    }
    44	}
    45	
    46	fn is_bound_non_empty(bound: &Bound<Bytes>) -> bool {
    47	    match bound {
    48	        Included(b) | Excluded(b) => !b.is_empty(),
    49	        Unbounded => true,
    50	    }
    51	}
    52	
    53	impl BytesRange {
    54	    pub(crate) fn new(start_bound: Bound<Bytes>, end_bound: Bound<Bytes>) -> Self {
    55	        assert!(
    56	            is_bound_non_empty(&start_bound),
    57	            "Start bound must be non-empty"
    58	        );
    59	        assert!(
    60	            is_bound_non_empty(&end_bound),
    61	            "End bound must be non-empty"
    62	        );
    63	        let inner = ComparableRange::new(start_bound, end_bound);
    64	        assert!(inner.non_empty(), "Range must be non-empty");
    65	        Self { inner }
    66	    }
    67	
    68	    pub(crate) fn new_empty() -> Self {
    69	        Self {
    70	            inner: ComparableRange::new(
    71	                Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(&[0_u8])),
    72	                Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(&[0_u8])),
    73	            ),
    74	        }
    75	    }
    76	
    77	    pub(crate) fn from<T: RangeBounds<Bytes>>(range: T) -> Self {
    78	        Self::new(range.start_bound().cloned(), range.end_bound().cloned())
    79	    }
    80	
    81	    pub(crate) fn from_slice<'a, T>(range: T) -> Self
    82	    where
    83	        T: RangeBounds<&'a [u8]>,
    84	    {
    85	        Self::new(
    86	            range.start_bound().map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b)),
    87	            range.end_bound().map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b)),
    88	        )
    89	    }
    90	
    91	    /// Build a half-open range `[prefix, prefix+1)` covering all keys that start with
    92	    /// `prefix`.
    93	    ///
    94	    /// - Empty prefix returns `(..)` so callers can scan the entire keyspace.
    95	    /// - If the prefix is all `0xff`, the end bound is unbounded rather than overflowing.
    96	    pub(crate) fn from_prefix(prefix: &[u8]) -> Self {
    97	        if prefix.is_empty() {
    98	            return Self::new(Unbounded, Unbounded);
    99	        }
   100	
   101	        let start = Bytes::copy_from_slice(prefix);
   102	        let end = Self::increment_prefix(prefix)
   103	            .map(Excluded)
   104	            .unwrap_or(Unbounded);
   105	        Self::new(Included(start), end)
   106	    }
   107	
   108	    /// Compute the smallest byte string that is lexicographically greater than any key
   109	    /// starting with `prefix`. Returns `None` when `prefix` is all `0xff`.
   110	    fn increment_prefix(prefix: &[u8]) -> Option<Bytes> {
   111	        let mut upper_bound = prefix.to_vec();
   112	
   113	        for i in (0..upper_bound.len()).rev() {
   114	            if upper_bound[i] != u8::MAX {
   115	                upper_bound[i] += 1;
   116	                upper_bound.truncate(i + 1);
   117	                return Some(Bytes::from(upper_bound));
   118	            }
   119	        }
   120	
   121	        None
   122	    }
   123	
   124	    #[cfg(test)]
   125	    pub(crate) fn from_ref<K, T>(range: T) -> Self
   126	    where
   127	        K: AsRef<[u8]>,
   128	        T: RangeBounds<K>,
   129	    {
   130	        let start = range
   131	            .start_bound()
   132	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   133	        let end = range
   134	            .end_bound()
   135	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   136	        Self::new(start, end)
   137	    }
   138	
   139	    pub(crate) fn intersect(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   140	        self.inner
   141	            .intersect(&other.inner)
   142	            .map(|inner| Self { inner })
   143	    }
   144	
   145	    pub(crate) fn is_start_bound_included_or_unbounded(&self) -> bool {
   146	        !matches!(self.start_bound(), Excluded(_))
   147	    }
   148	
   149	    #[cfg(test)]
   150	    pub(crate) fn non_empty(&self) -> bool {
   151	        self.inner.non_empty()
   152	    }
   153	
   154	    #[cfg(test)]
   155	    pub(crate) fn empty(&self) -> bool {
   156	        !self.inner.non_empty()
   157	    }
   158	
   159	    pub(crate) fn comparable_start_bound(&self) -> StartBound<&Bytes> {
   160	        self.inner.comparable_start_bound()
   161	    }
   162	
   163	    pub(crate) fn comparable_end_bound(&self) -> EndBound<&Bytes> {
   164	        self.inner.comparable_end_bound()
   165	    }
   166	
   167	    pub(crate) fn as_point(&self) -> Option<&Bytes> {
   168	        match (self.start_bound(), self.end_bound()) {
   169	            (Bound::Included(start), Bound::Included(end)) if start == end => Some(start),
   170	            _ => None,
   171	        }
   172	    }
   173	}

   250	    fn test_from_prefix_filters_keys_by_prefix() {
   251	        proptest!(|(
   252	            prefix in arbitrary::nonempty_bytes(8),
   253	            suffix in arbitrary::bytes(8)
   254	        )| {
   255	            let range = BytesRange::from_prefix(&prefix);
   256	
   257	            // Any key starting with the prefix should be contained.
   258	            let mut prefixed = prefix.to_vec();
   259	            prefixed.extend_from_slice(&suffix);
   260	            let prefixed = Bytes::from(prefixed);
   261	            prop_assert!(range.contains(&prefixed));
   262	
   263	            // A key with a different first byte should be rejected.
   264	            let mut non_prefixed = prefix.to_vec();
   265	            non_prefixed[0] = non_prefixed[0].wrapping_add(1);
   266	            let non_prefixed = Bytes::from(non_prefixed);
   267	            prop_assert!(!range.contains(&non_prefixed));
   268	        });
   269	    }

   141	fn cmp_bound<T: Ord>(a: &Bound<T>, b: &Bound<T>, start: bool) -> Ordering {
   142	    match (a, b) {
   143	        (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Included(b)) | (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => {
   144	            a.cmp(b)
   145	        }
   146	        (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => match a.cmp(b) {
   147	            Ordering::Equal => {
   148	                if start {
   149	                    Ordering::Less
   150	                } else {
   151	                    Ordering::Greater
   152	                }
   153	            }
   154	            other => other,
   155	        },
   156	        (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Included(b)) => match a.cmp(b) {
   157	            Ordering::Equal => {
   158	                if start {
   159	                    Ordering::Greater
   160	                } else {
   161	                    Ordering::Less
   162	                }
   163	            }
   164	            other => other,
   165	        },
   166	        (Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Unbounded) => Ordering::Equal,
   167	        (Bound::Unbounded, _) => {
   168	            if start {
   169	                Ordering::Less
   170	            } else {
   171	                Ordering::Greater
   172	            }
   173	        }
   174	        (_, Bound::Unbounded) => {
   175	            if start {
   176	                Ordering::Greater
   177	            } else {
   178	                Ordering::Less
   179	            }
   180	        }
   181	    }
   182	}

   188	}

   204	        let mut seq = serializer.serialize_struct("ComparableRange", 2)?;

   212	    fn hash<H: Hasher>(&self, state: &mut H) {
   213	        self.start.hash(state);
   214	        self.end.hash(state);
   215	    }
   216	}
   217	
   218	impl<T: Ord + Clone> ComparableRange<T> {
   219	    #[cfg(test)]
   220	    pub(crate) fn from_range<R: RangeBounds<T>>(range: R) -> Self {
   221	        Self::new(range.start_bound().cloned(), range.end_bound().cloned())
   222	    }
   223	
   224	    pub(crate) fn intersect(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   225	        let max_start = max(&self.start, &other.start);
   226	        let min_end = min(&self.end, &other.end);
   227	        let intersection = Self {
   228	            start: max_start.clone(),
   229	            end: min_end.clone(),
   230	        };
   231	        if intersection.non_empty() {
   232	            Some(intersection)
   233	        } else {
   234	            None
   235	        }
   236	    }
   237	
   238	    #[allow(dead_code)]
   239	    pub(crate) fn union(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   240	        // Sort the ranges to make the function commutative
   241	        let (first, second) = if self < other {
   242	            (self, other)
   243	        } else {
   244	            (other, self)
   245	        };
   246	        // If the ranges are not intersecting and they are not adjacent, no union is possible
   247	        if first.intersect(second).is_none() && !first.are_adjacent(second) {
   248	            return None;
   249	        }
   250	        // Take the minimum of start bounds and maximum of end bounds
   251	        Some(Self {
   252	            start: min(&first.start, &other.start).clone(),
   253	            end: max(&first.end, &second.end).clone(),
   254	        })
   255	    }
   256	
   257	    fn are_adjacent(&self, other: &Self) -> bool {
   258	        match (&self.end.inner, &other.start.inner) {
   259	            (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => a == b,
   260	            (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Included(b)) => a == b,
   261	            _ => false,
   262	        }
   263	    }
   264	
   265	    pub(crate) fn non_empty(&self) -> bool {
   266	        match (&self.start.inner, &self.end.inner) {
   267	            (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Included(b)) => a <= b,
   268	            (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => a < b,
   269	            (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => a < b,
   270	            (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Included(b)) => a < b,
   271	            (Bound::Unbounded, _) => true,
   272	            (_, Bound::Unbounded) => true,
   273	        }
   274	    }
   275	
   276	    pub(crate) fn comparable_start_bound(&self) -> StartBound<&T> {
   277	        StartBound {
   278	            inner: self.start_bound(),
   279	        }
   280	    }
   281	
   282	    pub(crate) fn comparable_end_bound(&self) -> EndBound<&T> {
   283	        EndBound {
   284	            inner: self.end_bound(),
   285	        }
   286	    }
   287	}
   288	
   289	impl<T: Ord + Clone> Clone for ComparableRange<T> {
   290	    fn clone(&self) -> Self {
   291	        Self::new(self.start.inner.clone(), self.end.inner.clone())
   292	    }
   293	}

   312	
   313	    use rand::seq::SliceRandom;
   314	    use rstest::rstest;
   315	
   316	    use crate::comparable_range::{ComparableRange, EndBound, StartBound};
   317	
   318	    struct TestCase(Bound<u32>, Bound<u32>, Ordering);
   319	
   320	    #[rstest]
   321	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Included(1), Ordering::Equal))]
   322	    // [1, 100) vs. (1, 100) => (1 <= n < 100) vs. (1 < n < 100)
   323	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Excluded(1), Ordering::Less))]
   324	    // (1, 100) vs. [1, 100) =>  (1 < n < 100) vs. (1 <= n < 100)
   325	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Included(1), Ordering::Greater))]
   326	    // For start bound, unbounded represents -Inf
   327	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Included(1), Ordering::Less))]
   328	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Excluded(1), Ordering::Less))]
   329	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Unbounded, Ordering::Greater))]
   330	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Unbounded, Ordering::Greater))]
   331	    fn test_start_bound_cmp(#[case] test_case: TestCase) {
   332	        let lhs = StartBound::from(test_case.0);
   333	        let rhs = StartBound::from(test_case.1);
   334	        assert_eq!(lhs.cmp(&rhs), test_case.2);
   335	    }
   336	
   337	    #[rstest]
   338	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(100), Bound::Included(100), Ordering::Equal))]
   339	    // (1, 100] vs. (1, 100) => (1 < n <= 100) vs. (1 < n < 100)
   340	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(100), Bound::Excluded(100), Ordering::Greater))]
   341	    // (1, 100) vs. (1, 100] =>  (1 < n < 100) vs. (1 < n <= 100)
   342	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Excluded(100), Bound::Included(100), Ordering::Less))]
   343	    // For end bound, unbounded represents +Inf
   344	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Included(1), Ordering::Greater))]
   345	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Excluded(1), Ordering::Greater))]
   346	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Unbounded, Ordering::Less))]
   347	    #[case(TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Unbounded, Ordering::Less))]
   348	    fn test_end_bound_cmp(#[case] test_case: TestCase) {
   349	        let lhs = EndBound::from(test_case.0);
   350	        let rhs = EndBound::from(test_case.1);
   351	        assert_eq!(lhs.cmp(&rhs), test_case.2);
   352	    }
   353	
   354	    #[test]
   355	    fn test_range() {
   356	        let ranges = vec![
   357	            ComparableRange::from_range(..10),
   358	            ComparableRange::from_range(..1000),
   359	            ComparableRange::from_range(..),
   360	            ComparableRange::from_range(1..5),
   361	            ComparableRange::from_range(1..10),
   362	            ComparableRange::from_range(1..),
   363	            ComparableRange::from_range(2..3),
   364	            ComparableRange::from_range(2..),
   365	            ComparableRange::from_range(100..123),
   366	        ];
   367	        let mut shuffled_ranges = ranges.clone();
   368	        // Shuffle the ranges to ensure the order is random
   369	        shuffled_ranges.shuffle(&mut rand::rng());
   370	        // Sort the ranges to ensure the order is deterministic
   371	        shuffled_ranges.sort();
   372	
   373	        assert_eq!(shuffled_ranges, ranges);
   374	    }
   375	
   376	    struct TwoRangeOperation<T: Ord + Clone> {
   377	        first: ComparableRange<T>,
   378	        second: ComparableRange<T>,
   379	        result: Option<ComparableRange<T>>,
   380	    }
   381	
   382	    impl<T: Ord + Clone> TwoRangeOperation<T> {
   383	        fn some<R1, R2, RI>(first: R1, second: R2, intersection: RI) -> Self
   384	        where
   385	            R1: RangeBounds<T>,
   386	            R2: RangeBounds<T>,
   387	            RI: RangeBounds<T>,
   388	        {
   389	            Self {
   390	                first: ComparableRange::from_range(first),
   391	                second: ComparableRange::from_range(second),
   392	                result: Some(ComparableRange::from_range(intersection)),
   393	            }
   394	        }
   395	
   396	        fn none<R1, R2>(first: R1, second: R2) -> Self
   397	        where
   398	            R1: RangeBounds<T>,
   399	            R2: RangeBounds<T>,
   400	        {
   401	            Self {
   402	                first: ComparableRange::from_range(first),
   403	                second: ComparableRange::from_range(second),
   404	                result: None,
   405	            }
   406	        }
   407	    }
   408	
   409	    #[rstest]
   410	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(0..10, 0..10, 0..10))]
   411	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(0..10, 1..10, 1..10))]
   412	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(0..10, 0..9, 0..9))]
   413	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(0..10, 0..=9, 0..=9))]
   414	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(..=1337, 10..15, 10..15))]
   415	    #[allow(clippy::reversed_empty_ranges)]
   416	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::none(50..40, 10..60))]
   417	    fn test_intersection(#[case] test_case: TwoRangeOperation<u32>) {
   418	        for (first, second) in [
   419	            (&test_case.first, &test_case.second),
   420	            (&test_case.second, &test_case.first),
   421	        ] {
   422	            let intersection = first.intersect(second);
   423	            assert_eq!(intersection, test_case.result);
   424	        }
   425	    }
   426	
   427	    #[rstest]
   428	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(0..10, 10..100, 0..100))]
   429	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(0..=10, 10..100, 0..100))]
   430	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::none(0..10, 11..100))]
   431	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(..100, 5..=100, ..=100))]
   432	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(..100, 5.., ..))]
   433	    #[case(TwoRangeOperation::some(0..=10, (Bound::Excluded(10), Bound::Included(100)), 0..=100))]
   434	    #[allow(clippy::reversed_empty_ranges)]
   435	    #[case::empty_range(TwoRangeOperation::none(5..0, 0..10))]
   436	    #[case::empty_range(TwoRangeOperation::none((Bound::Excluded(5), Bound::Excluded(5)), 0..10))]
   437	    fn test_union(#[case] test_case: TwoRangeOperation<u32>) {
   438	        for (first, second) in [
   439	            (&test_case.first, &test_case.second),
   440	            (&test_case.second, &test_case.first),
   441	        ] {
   442	            let union = first.union(second);
   443	            assert_eq!(union, test_case.result);
   444	        }
   445	    }
   446	
   447	    #[test]
   448	    fn test_is_non_empty() {
   449	        struct TestCase(Bound<i32>, Bound<i32>, bool);
   450	        let cases = vec![
   451	            TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Included(1), true),
   452	            TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Excluded(1), false),
   453	            TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Included(1), false),
   454	            TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Excluded(1), false),
   455	            TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Excluded(2), true),
   456	            TestCase(Bound::Excluded(2), Bound::Excluded(1), false),
   457	            TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Included(1), true),
   458	            TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Excluded(1), true),
   459	            TestCase(Bound::Included(1), Bound::Unbounded, true),
   460	            TestCase(Bound::Excluded(1), Bound::Unbounded, true),
   461	            TestCase(Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Unbounded, true),
   462	        ];
   463	        for case in cases {
   464	            assert_eq!(ComparableRange::new(case.0, case.1).non_empty(), case.2);
   465	        }
   466	    }

The `is_bound_non_empty` function checks if a bound value is empty (i.e., `Bytes::is_empty()`). The PR description says that users might supply `RangeBounds<Bytes>` that have empty start or ending bounds (an empty bytes array `[]`). Currently, `BytesRange::new` asserts that bounds must be non-empty, which throws/panics when empty bounds are supplied.

The fix should change `BytesRange` to accept empty bounds. Let me look at how this is used and what the PR description suggests.

     1	use bytes::Bytes;
     2	use serde::Serialize;
     3	use std::ops::Bound::{Excluded, Included, Unbounded};
     4	use std::ops::{Bound, RangeBounds};
     5	
     6	use crate::comparable_range::{ComparableRange, EndBound, StartBound};
     7	
     8	/// Concrete struct representing a range of Bytes. Gets around much of
     9	/// the cumbersome work associated with the generic trait RangeBounds<Bytes>
    10	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq, Ord, PartialOrd, Hash)]
    11	pub(crate) struct BytesRange {
    12	    inner: ComparableRange<Bytes>,
    13	}
    14	
    15	impl Serialize for BytesRange {
    16	    fn serialize<S>(&self, serializer: S) -> Result<S::Ok, S::Error>
    17	    where
    18	        S: serde::Serializer,
    19	    {
    20	        self.inner.serialize(serializer)
    21	    }
    22	}
    23	
    24	#[cfg(test)]
    25	// Checks for the annoying case when we have ("prefix", "prefix\0").
    26	// When both bounds are excluded, the range is empty even though
    27	// "prefix" < "prefix\0".
    28	pub(crate) fn is_prefix_increment(prefix: &[u8], b: &[u8]) -> bool {
    29	    if !b.starts_with(prefix.as_ref()) {
    30	        return false;
    31	    }
    32	
    33	    b[prefix.len()..] == [u8::MIN]
    34	}
    35	
    36	impl RangeBounds<Bytes> for BytesRange {
    37	    fn start_bound(&self) -> Bound<&Bytes> {
    38	        self.inner.start_bound()
    39	    }
    40	
    41	    fn end_bound(&self) -> Bound<&Bytes> {
    42	        self.inner.end_bound()
    43	    }
    44	}
    45	
    46	fn is_bound_non_empty(bound: &Bound<Bytes>) -> bool {
    47	    match bound {
    48	        Included(b) | Excluded(b) => !b.is_empty(),
    49	        Unbounded => true,
    50	    }
    51	}
    52	
    53	impl BytesRange {
    54	    pub(crate) fn new(start_bound: Bound<Bytes>, end_bound: Bound<Bytes>) -> Self {
    55	        assert!(
    56	            is_bound_non_empty(&start_bound),
    57	            "Start bound must be non-empty"
    58	        );
    59	        assert!(
    60	            is_bound_non_empty(&end_bound),
    61	            "End bound must be non-empty"
    62	        );
    63	        let inner = ComparableRange::new(start_bound, end_bound);
    64	        assert!(inner.non_empty(), "Range must be non-empty");
    65	        Self { inner }
    66	    }
    67	
    68	    pub(crate) fn new_empty() -> Self {
    69	        Self {
    70	            inner: ComparableRange::new(
    71	                Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(&[0_u8])),
    72	                Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(&[0_u8])),
    73	            ),
    74	        }
    75	    }
    76	
    77	    pub(crate) fn from<T: RangeBounds<Bytes>>(range: T) -> Self {
    78	        Self::new(range.start_bound().cloned(), range.end_bound().cloned())
    79	    }
    80	
    81	    pub(crate) fn from_slice<'a, T>(range: T) -> Self
    82	    where
    83	        T: RangeBounds<&'a [u8]>,
    84	    {
    85	        Self::new(
    86	            range.start_bound().map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b)),
    87	            range.end_bound().map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b)),
    88	        )
    89	    }
    90	
    91	    /// Build a half-open range `[prefix, prefix+1)` covering all keys that start with
    92	    /// `prefix`.
    93	    ///
    94	    /// - Empty prefix returns `(..)` so callers can scan the entire keyspace.
    95	    /// - If the prefix is all `0xff`, the end bound is unbounded rather than overflowing.
    96	    pub(crate) fn from_prefix(prefix: &[u8]) -> Self {
    97	        if prefix.is_empty() {
    98	            return Self::new(Unbounded, Unbounded);
    99	        }
   100	
   101	        let start = Bytes::copy_from_slice(prefix);
   102	        let end = Self::increment_prefix(prefix)
   103	            .map(Excluded)
   104	            .unwrap_or(Unbounded);
   105	        Self::new(Included(start), end)
   106	    }
   107	
   108	    /// Compute the smallest byte string that is lexicographically greater than any key
   109	    /// starting with `prefix`. Returns `None` when `prefix` is all `0xff`.
   110	    fn increment_prefix(prefix: &[u8]) -> Option<Bytes> {
   111	        let mut upper_bound = prefix.to_vec();
   112	
   113	        for i in (0..upper_bound.len()).rev() {
   114	            if upper_bound[i] != u8::MAX {
   115	                upper_bound[i] += 1;
   116	                upper_bound.truncate(i + 1);
   117	                return Some(Bytes::from(upper_bound));
   118	            }
   119	        }
   120	
   121	        None
   122	    }
   123	
   124	    #[cfg(test)]
   125	    pub(crate) fn from_ref<K, T>(range: T) -> Self
   126	    where
   127	        K: AsRef<[u8]>,
   128	        T: RangeBounds<K>,
   129	    {
   130	        let start = range
   131	            .start_bound()
   132	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   133	        let end = range
   134	            .end_bound()
   135	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   136	        Self::new(start, end)
   137	    }
   138	
   139	    pub(crate) fn intersect(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   140	        self.inner
   141	            .intersect(&other.inner)
   142	            .map(|inner| Self { inner })
   143	    }
   144	
   145	    pub(crate) fn is_start_bound_included_or_unbounded(&self) -> bool {
   146	        !matches!(self.start_bound(), Excluded(_))
   147	    }
   148	
   149	    #[cfg(test)]
   150	    pub(crate) fn non_empty(&self) -> bool {
   151	        self.inner.non_empty()
   152	    }
   153	
   154	    #[cfg(test)]
   155	    pub(crate) fn empty(&self) -> bool {
   156	        !self.inner.non_empty()
   157	    }
   158	
   159	    pub(crate) fn comparable_start_bound(&self) -> StartBound<&Bytes> {
   160	        self.inner.comparable_start_bound()
   161	    }
   162	
   163	    pub(crate) fn comparable_end_bound(&self) -> EndBound<&Bytes> {
   164	        self.inner.comparable_end_bound()
   165	    }
   166	
   167	    pub(crate) fn as_point(&self) -> Option<&Bytes> {
   168	        match (self.start_bound(), self.end_bound()) {
   169	            (Bound::Included(start), Bound::Included(end)) if start == end => Some(start),
   170	            _ => None,
   171	        }
   172	    }
   173	}

   141	fn cmp_bound<T: Ord>(a: &Bound<T>, b: &Bound<T>, start: bool) -> Ordering {
   142	    match (a, b) {
   143	        (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Included(b)) | (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => {
   144	            a.cmp(b)
   145	        }
   146	        (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => match a.cmp(b) {
   147	            Ordering::Equal => {
   148	                if start {
   149	                    Ordering::Less
   150	                } else {
   151	                    Ordering::Greater
   152	                }
   153	            }
   154	            other => other,
   155	        },
   156	        (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Included(b)) => match a.cmp(b) {
   157	            Ordering::Equal => {
   158	                if start {
   159	                    Ordering::Greater
   160	                } else {
   161	                    Ordering::Less
   162	                }
   163	            }
   164	            other => other,
   165	        },
   166	        (Bound::Unbounded, Bound::Unbounded) => Ordering::Equal,
   167	        (Bound::Unbounded, _) => {
   168	            if start {
   169	                Ordering::Less
   170	            } else {
   171	                Ordering::Greater
   172	            }
   173	        }
   174	        (_, Bound::Unbounded) => {
   175	            if start {
   176	                Ordering::Greater
   177	            } else {
   178	                Ordering::Less
   179	            }
   180	        }
   181	    }
   182	}

   184	#[derive(Debug, Eq, PartialEq, Ord, PartialOrd)]
   185	pub(crate) struct ComparableRange<T: Ord> {
   186	    start: StartBound<T>,
   187	    end: EndBound<T>,
   188	}
   189	
   190	impl<T: Ord> ComparableRange<T> {
   191	    pub(crate) fn new(start: Bound<T>, end: Bound<T>) -> Self {
   192	        Self {
   193	            start: StartBound::from(start),
   194	            end: EndBound::from(end),
   195	        }
   196	    }
   197	}

   200	    fn serialize<S>(&self, serializer: S) -> Result<S::Ok, S::Error>
   201	    where
   202	        S: Serializer,
   203	    {
   204	        let mut seq = serializer.serialize_struct("ComparableRange", 2)?;
   205	        seq.serialize_field("start", &self.start)?;
   206	        seq.serialize_field("end", &self.end)?;
   207	        seq.end()
   208	    }
   209	}
   210	
   211	impl<T: Ord + Hash> Hash for ComparableRange<T> {
   212	    fn hash<H: Hasher>(&self, state: &mut H) {
   213	        self.start.hash(state);
   214	        self.end.hash(state);
   215	    }
   216	}
   217	
   218	impl<T: Ord + Clone> ComparableRange<T> {
   219	    #[cfg(test)]
   220	    pub(crate) fn from_range<R: RangeBounds<T>>(range: R) -> Self {
   221	        Self::new(range.start_bound().cloned(), range.end_bound().cloned())
   222	    }
   223	
   224	    pub(crate) fn intersect(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   225	        let max_start = max(&self.start, &other.start);
   226	        let min_end = min(&self.end, &other.end);
   227	        let intersection = Self {
   228	            start: max_start.clone(),
   229	            end: min_end.clone(),
   230	        };
   231	        if intersection.non_empty() {
   232	            Some(intersection)
   233	        } else {
   234	            None
   235	        }
   236	    }
   237	
   238	    #[allow(dead_code)]
   239	    pub(crate) fn union(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   240	        // Sort the ranges to make the function commutative
   241	        let (first, second) = if self < other {
   242	            (self, other)
   243	        } else {
   244	            (other, self)
   245	        };
   246	        // If the ranges are not intersecting and they are not adjacent, no union is possible
   247	        if first.intersect(second).is_none() && !first.are_adjacent(second) {
   248	            return None;
   249	        }
   250	        // Take the minimum of start bounds and maximum of end bounds
   251	        Some(Self {
   252	            start: min(&first.start, &other.start).clone(),
   253	            end: max(&first.end, &second.end).clone(),
   254	        })
   255	    }
   256	
   257	    fn are_adjacent(&self, other: &Self) -> bool {
   258	        match (&self.end.inner, &other.start.inner) {
   259	            (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => a == b,
   260	            (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Included(b)) => a == b,
   261	            _ => false,
   262	        }
   263	    }
   264	
   265	    pub(crate) fn non_empty(&self) -> bool {
   266	        match (&self.start.inner, &self.end.inner) {
   267	            (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Included(b)) => a <= b,
   268	            (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => a < b,
   269	            (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => a < b,
   270	            (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Included(b)) => a < b,
   271	            (Bound::Unbounded, _) => true,
   272	            (_, Bound::Unbounded) => true,
   273	        }
   274	    }
   275	
   276	    pub(crate) fn comparable_start_bound(&self) -> StartBound<&T> {
   277	        StartBound {
   278	            inner: self.start_bound(),
   279	        }
   280	    }
   281	
   282	    pub(crate) fn comparable_end_bound(&self) -> EndBound<&T> {
   283	        EndBound {
   284	            inner: self.end_bound(),
   285	        }
   286	    }
   287	}
   288	
   289	impl<T: Ord + Clone> Clone for ComparableRange<T> {
   290	    fn clone(&self) -> Self {
   291	        Self::new(self.start.inner.clone(), self.end.inner.clone())
   292	    }
   293	}

    66	/// A wrapper around a `Bytes` buffer containing a FlatBuffer-encoded `SsTableIndex`.

    68	pub(crate) struct SsTableIndexOwned {
    69	    data: Bytes,
    70	}
    71	
    72	impl SsTableIndexOwned {
    73	    pub(crate) fn new(data: Bytes) -> Result<Self, InvalidFlatbuffer> {
    74	        flatbuffers::root_with_opts::<SsTableIndex>(&verifier_options(), &data)?;
    75	        Ok(Self { data })
    76	    }
    77	
    78	    pub(crate) fn borrow(&self) -> SsTableIndex<'_> {
    79	        let raw = &self.data;
    80	        unsafe { flatbuffers::root_unchecked::<SsTableIndex>(raw) }
    81	    }
    82	
    83	    pub(crate) fn data(&self) -> Bytes {
    84	        self.data.clone()
    85	    }
    86	
    87	    pub(crate) fn clamp_allocated_size(&self) -> Self {
    88	        Self::new(clamp_allocated_size_bytes(&self.data))
    89	            .expect("clamped buffer could not be decoded to index")
    90	    }
    91	
    92	    /// Returns the size of the SSTable index in bytes.
    93	    pub(crate) fn size(&self) -> usize {
    94	        self.data.len()
    95	    }
    96	}

   108	#[derive(Clone)]
   109	pub(crate) struct FlatBufferSsTableInfoCodec {}
   110	
   111	impl SsTableInfoCodec for FlatBufferSsTableInfoCodec {
   112	    fn encode(&self, info: &SsTableInfo) -> Bytes {
   113	        Self::create_from_sst_info(info)
   114	    }
   115	
   116	    fn decode(&self, bytes: &Bytes) -> Result<SsTableInfo, SlateDBError> {
   117	        let info = flatbuffers::root_with_opts::<FbSsTableInfo>(&verifier_options(), bytes)?;
   118	        Ok(Self::sst_info(&info))
   119	    }
   120	
   121	    fn clone_box(&self) -> Box<dyn SsTableInfoCodec> {
   122	        Box::new(Self {})
   123	    }
   124	}
   125	
   126	impl FlatBufferSsTableInfoCodec {
   127	    pub(crate) fn sst_info(info: &FbSsTableInfo) -> SsTableInfo {
   128	        let first_entry: Option<Bytes> = info
   129	            .first_entry()
   130	            .map(|entry| Bytes::copy_from_slice(entry.bytes()));
   131	        let last_entry: Option<Bytes> = info
   132	            .last_entry()
   133	            .map(|entry| Bytes::copy_from_slice(entry.bytes()));
   134	
   135	        SsTableInfo {
   136	            first_entry,
   137	            last_entry,
   138	            index_offset: info.index_offset(),
   139	            index_len: info.index_len(),
   140	            filter_offset: info.filter_offset(),
   141	            filter_len: info.filter_len(),
   142	            compression_codec: info.compression_format().into(),
   143	            sst_type: info.sst_type().into(),
   144	            stats_offset: info.stats_offset(),
   145	            stats_len: info.stats_len(),
   146	        }
   147	    }
   148	
   149	    pub(crate) fn create_from_sst_info(info: &SsTableInfo) -> Bytes {
   150	        let builder = FlatBufferBuilder::new();
   151	        let mut db_fb_builder = DbFlatBufferBuilder::new(builder);
   152	        db_fb_builder.create_sst_info(info)
   153	    }
   154	}
   155	
   156	pub(crate) struct FlatBufferManifestCodec {}
   157	
   158	impl ObjectCodec<Manifest> for FlatBufferManifestCodec {
   159	    fn encode(&self, manifest: &Manifest) -> Bytes {
   160	        Self::create_from_manifest_v1(manifest)
   161	    }
   162	
   163	    fn decode(&self, bytes: &Bytes) -> Result<Manifest, Box<dyn std::error::Error + Send + Sync>> {
   164	        if bytes.len() < 2 {
   165	            return Err(Box::new(SlateDBError::EmptyManifest));
   166	        }
   167	        let version = u16::from_be_bytes([bytes[0], bytes[1]]);
   168	        let unversioned_bytes = bytes.slice(2..);
   169	        match version {
   170	            1 => {
   171	                let manifest = flatbuffers::root_with_opts::<ManifestV1>(
   172	                    &verifier_options(),
   173	                    unversioned_bytes.as_ref(),
   174	                )?;
   175	                Self::manifest_v1(&manifest)
   176	            }
   177	            2 => {
   178	                let manifest = flatbuffers::root_with_opts::<ManifestV2>(
   179	                    &verifier_options(),
   180	                    unversioned_bytes.as_ref(),
   181	                )?;
   182	                Self::manifest_v2(&manifest)
   183	            }
   184	            _ => Err(Box::new(SlateDBError::InvalidVersion {
   185	                format_name: "manifest",
   186	                supported_versions: vec![1, 2],
   187	                actual_version: version,
   188	            })),
   189	        }
   190	    }
   191	}
   192	
   193	impl FlatBufferManifestCodec {
   194	    fn decode_uuid(uuid: Uuid) -> uuid::Uuid {
   195	        uuid::Uuid::from_u64_pair(uuid.high(), uuid.low())
   196	    }
   197	
   198	    fn decode_bytes_range(range: root_generated::BytesRange) -> BytesRange {
   199	        let start_key = Self::decode_bytes_bound(range.start_bound());
   200	        let end_key = Self::decode_bytes_bound(range.end_bound());
   201	        BytesRange::new(start_key, end_key)
   202	    }
   203	
   204	    fn decode_bytes_bound(bound: root_generated::BytesBound) -> Bound<Bytes> {
   205	        match (bound.bound_type(), bound.key()) {
   206	            (BoundType::Included, Some(key)) => {
   207	                Bound::Included(Bytes::copy_from_slice(key.bytes()))
   208	            }
   209	            (BoundType::Excluded, Some(key)) => {
   210	                Bound::Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(key.bytes()))
   211	            }
   212	            (BoundType::Unbounded, None) => Bound::Unbounded,
   213	            (bound_type, key) => {
   214	                unreachable!("Unsupported bound type: {:?}, key: {:?}", bound_type, key)
   215	            }
   216	        }
   217	    }
   218	
   219	    // ManifestV1 has no view IDs, so we use SST IDs during migration.
   220	    // This also allows to use l0_last_compacted from V1 which is an SST ID rather than SST view ID.
   221	    #[allow(clippy::disallowed_methods)]
   222	    pub(crate) fn manifest_v1(
   223	        manifest: &ManifestV1,
   224	    ) -> Result<Manifest, Box<dyn std::error::Error + Send + Sync>> {
   225	        let l0_last_compacted = manifest.l0_last_compacted().map(|id| id.ulid());
   226	        let mut l0 = VecDeque::new();
   227	
   228	        for man_sst in manifest.l0().iter() {
   229	            let sst_ulid = man_sst.id().ulid();
   230	            let format_version = man_sst
   231	                .format_version()
   232	                .unwrap_or(ORIGINAL_SST_FORMAT_VERSION);
   233	            let sst_info = FlatBufferSsTableInfoCodec::sst_info(&man_sst.info());
   234	            let handle = SsTableHandle::new(Compacted(sst_ulid), format_version, sst_info);
   235	            let l0_sst = SsTableView::new_projected(
   236	                sst_ulid,
   237	                handle,
   238	                man_sst.visible_range().map(Self::decode_bytes_range),
   239	            );
   240	            l0.push_back(l0_sst);
   241	        }
   242	        let mut compacted = Vec::new();
   243	        for manifest_sr in manifest.compacted().iter() {
   244	            let mut ssts = Vec::new();
   245	            for manifest_sst in manifest_sr.ssts().iter() {
   246	                let sst_ulid = manifest_sst.id().ulid();
   247	                let format_version = manifest_sst
   248	                    .format_version()
   249	                    .unwrap_or(ORIGINAL_SST_FORMAT_VERSION);
   250	                let info = FlatBufferSsTableInfoCodec::sst_info(&manifest_sst.info());
   251	                let handle = SsTableHandle::new(Compacted(sst_ulid), format_version, info);
   252	                ssts.push(SsTableView::new_projected(
   253	                    sst_ulid,
   254	                    handle,
   255	                    manifest_sst.visible_range().map(Self::decode_bytes_range),
   256	                ));
   257	            }
   258	            compacted.push(db_state::SortedRun {
   259	                id: manifest_sr.id(),
   260	                sst_views: ssts,
   261	            })
   262	        }
   263	        let checkpoints: Vec<checkpoint::Checkpoint> = manifest
   264	            .checkpoints()
   265	            .iter()
   266	            .map(|cp| checkpoint::Checkpoint {
   267	                id: Self::decode_uuid(cp.id()),
   268	                manifest_id: cp.manifest_id(),
   269	                expire_time: match cp.checkpoint_expire_time_s() {
   270	                    0 => None,
   271	                    _ => Some(
   272	                        DateTime::<Utc>::from_timestamp(cp.checkpoint_expire_time_s() as i64, 0)
   273	                            .expect("invalid timestamp"),
   274	                    ),
   275	                },
   276	                create_time: DateTime::<Utc>::from_timestamp(
   277	                    cp.checkpoint_create_time_s() as i64,
   278	                    0,
   279	                )
   280	                .expect("invalid timestamp"),
   281	                name: cp.name().map(|s| s.to_string()),
   282	            })
   283	            .collect();
   284	        let sequence_tracker = match manifest.sequence_tracker() {
   285	            Some(bytes) => SequenceTracker::from_bytes(bytes.bytes())
   286	                .expect("Invalid encoding of sequence tracker in manifest."),
   287	            None => SequenceTracker::new(),
   288	        };
   289	        let core = ManifestCore {
   290	            initialized: manifest.initialized(),
   291	            // In V1, view IDs are SST IDs, so both fields are the same.
   292	            last_compacted_l0_sst_view_id: l0_last_compacted,
   293	            last_compacted_l0_sst_id: l0_last_compacted,
   294	            l0,
   295	            compacted,
   296	            next_wal_sst_id: manifest.wal_id_last_seen() + 1,
   297	            replay_after_wal_id: manifest.replay_after_wal_id(),
   298	            last_l0_seq: manifest.last_l0_seq(),
   299	            last_l0_clock_tick: manifest.last_l0_clock_tick(),
   300	            checkpoints,
   301	            wal_object_store_uri: manifest.wal_object_store_uri().map(|uri| uri.to_string()),
   302	            recent_snapshot_min_seq: manifest.recent_snapshot_min_seq(),
   303	            sequence_tracker,
   304	        };
   305	        let external_dbs = manifest.external_dbs().map(|external_dbs| {
   306	            external_dbs
   307	                .iter()
   308	                .map(|db| ExternalDb {
   309	                    path: db.path().to_string(),
   310	                    source_checkpoint_id: Self::decode_uuid(db.source_checkpoint_id()),
   311	                    final_checkpoint_id: db.final_checkpoint_id().map(|id| Self::decode_uuid(id)),
   312	                    sst_ids: db.sst_ids().iter().map(|id| Compacted(id.ulid())).collect(),
   313	                })
   314	                .collect()
   315	        });
   316	
   317	        Ok(Manifest {
   318	            external_dbs: external_dbs.unwrap_or_default(),
   319	            core,
   320	            writer_epoch: manifest.writer_epoch(),
   321	            compactor_epoch: manifest.compactor_epoch(),
   322	        })
   323	    }
   324	
   325	    fn decode_compacted_sst_view(
   326	        view: &CompactedSsTableView,
   327	        sst_lookup: &std::collections::HashMap<Ulid, SsTableHandle>,
   328	    ) -> Result<SsTableView, Box<dyn std::error::Error + Send + Sync>> {
   329	        let id = view.id().ulid();
   330	        let ulid = view.sst_id().ulid();
   331	        let handle = sst_lookup
   332	            .get(&ulid)
   333	            .ok_or_else(|| format!("CompactedSsTableView references unknown SST id: {ulid}"))?
   334	            .clone();
   335	        Ok(SsTableView::new_projected(
   336	            id,
   337	            handle,
   338	            view.visible_range().map(Self::decode_bytes_range),
   339	        ))
   340	    }
   341

   400	                .expect("Invalid encoding of sequence tracker in manifest."),

    19	/// A database transaction that provides atomic read-write operations with
    20	/// configurable isolation levels. This is the main interface for transactional
    21	/// operations in SlateDB.
    22	///
    23	/// # Examples
    24	///
    25	/// Basic transaction usage:
    26	/// ```rust
    27	/// # async fn run() -> Result<(), slatedb::Error> {
    28	/// #     use std::sync::Arc;
    29	/// #     use slatedb::object_store::memory::InMemory;
    30	/// use slatedb::{Db, IsolationLevel};
    31	///
    32	/// #     let object_store = Arc::new(InMemory::new());
    33	/// #     let db = Db::open("path/to/db", object_store).await?;
    34	/// let txn = db.begin(IsolationLevel::Snapshot).await?;
    35	///
    36	/// // Read operations
    37	/// let value = txn.get(b"key").await?;
    38	///
    39	/// // Write operations
    40	/// txn.put(b"key", b"value")?;
    41	/// txn.delete(b"key")?;
    42	///
    43	/// // Commit the transaction
    44	/// txn.commit().await?;
    45	/// # Ok(())
    46	/// # };
    47	/// ```
    48	pub struct DbTransaction {
    49	    /// Transaction ID generated by the transaction manager
    50	    txn_id: Uuid,
    51	    /// Sequence number when the transaction started
    52	    started_seq: u64,
    53	    /// Reference to the transaction manager
    54	    txn_manager: Arc<TransactionManager>,
    55	    /// The write batch of the transaction, which contains the uncommitted writes.
    56	    /// Users can read data from the write batch during the transaction, thus providing
    57	    /// an MVCC view of the database.
    58	    ///
    59	    /// DbTransaction is not intended for concurrent use; we use `RwLock` (not `RefCell`) for
    60	    /// interior mutability to preserve `Sync` in async contexts. `RefCell` is `!Sync` and would
    61	    /// make `DbTransaction` `!Sync`, which is incompatible with async code using the `DbRead`
    62	    /// trait.
    63	    write_batch: RwLock<WriteBatch>,
    64	    /// Reference to the database
    65	    db_inner: Arc<DbInner>,
    66	    /// Isolation level for this transaction
    67	    isolation_level: IsolationLevel,
    68	    /// Range trackers for scanned ranges (used for SSI conflict detection)
    69	    range_trackers: Mutex<Vec<Arc<DbIteratorRangeTracker>>>,
    70	    /// Keys that should be excluded from write conflict detection when committing.
    71	    untracked_write_keys: RwLock<HashSet<Bytes>>,
    72	}
    73	
    74	impl DbTransaction {
    75	    #[allow(unused)]
    76	    pub(crate) fn new(
    77	        db_inner: Arc<DbInner>,
    78	        txn_manager: Arc<TransactionManager>,
    79	        isolation_level: IsolationLevel,
    80	    ) -> Self {
    81	        let (txn_id, seq) = txn_manager.new_transaction();
    82	
    83	        Self {
    84	            txn_id,
    85	            started_seq: seq,
    86	            txn_manager,
    87	            write_batch: RwLock::new(WriteBatch::new().with_txn_id(txn_id)),
    88	            db_inner,
    89	            isolation_level,
    90	            range_trackers: Mutex::new(Vec::new()),
    91	            untracked_write_keys: RwLock::new(HashSet::new()),
    92	        }
    93	    }
    94	
    95	    /// Get a value from the transaction with default read options.
    96	    /// This operation will track the read for conflict detection in SSI mode.
    97	    ///
    98	    /// ## Arguments
    99	    /// - `key`: the key to get
   100	    ///
   101	    /// ## Returns
   102	    /// - `Result<Option<Bytes>, SlateDBError>`: the value if it exists, None otherwise
   103	    pub async fn get<K: AsRef<[u8]> + Send>(&self, key: K) -> Result<Option<Bytes>, crate::Error> {
   104	        self.get_with_options(key, &ReadOptions::default()).await
   105	    }
   106	
   107	    /// Get a value from the transaction with custom read options.
   108	    /// This operation will track the read for conflict detection in SSI mode.
   109	    ///
   110	    /// ## Arguments
   111	    /// - `key`: the key to get
   112	    /// - `options`: the read options to use
   113	    ///
   114	    /// ## Returns
   115	    /// - `Result<Option<Bytes>, SlateDBError>`: the value if it exists, None otherwise
   116	    pub async fn get_with_options<K: AsRef<[u8]> + Send>(
   117	        &self,
   118	        key: K,
   119	        options: &ReadOptions,
   120	    ) -> Result<Option<Bytes>, crate::Error> {
   121	        self.get_key_value_with_options(key, options)
   122	            .await
   123	            .map(|kv_opt| kv_opt.map(|kv| kv.value))
   124	    }
   125	
   126	    /// Get a key-value pair from the transaction with default read options.
   127	    pub async fn get_key_value<K: AsRef<[u8]> + Send>(
   128	        &self,
   129	        key: K,
   130	    ) -> Result<Option<KeyValue>, crate::Error> {
   131	        self.get_key_value_with_options(key, &ReadOptions::default())
   132	            .await
   133	    }
   134	
   135	    /// Get a key-value pair from the transaction with custom read options.
   136	    pub async fn get_key_value_with_options<K: AsRef<[u8]> + Send>(
   137	        &self,
   138	        key: K,
   139	        options: &ReadOptions,
   140	    ) -> Result<Option<KeyValue>, crate::Error> {
   141	        self.db_inner.check_closed()?;
   142	
   143	        // Track read key for SSI conflict detection if needed
   144	        if self.isolation_level == IsolationLevel::SerializableSnapshot {
   145	            let key_bytes = Bytes::copy_from_slice(key.as_ref());
   146	            let mut read_keys = HashSet::new();
   147	            read_keys.insert(key_bytes);
   148	            self.txn_manager.track_read_keys(&self.txn_id, read_keys);
   149	        }
   150	
   151	        let db_state = self.db_inner.state.read().view();
   152	
   153	        // Clone the WriteBatch for snapshot isolation
   154	        let write_batch_cloned = self.write_batch.read().clone();
   155	
   156	        // For now, delegate to the underlying reader
   157	        let kv = self
   158	            .db_inner
   159	            .reader
   160	            .get_key_value_with_options(
   161	                key,
   162	                options,
   163	                &db_state,
   164	                Some(write_batch_cloned),
   165	                Some(self.started_seq),
   166	            )
   167	            .await
   168	            .map_err(crate::Error::from)?;
   169	        Ok(kv)
   170	    }
   171	
   172	    /// Scan a range of keys using the default scan options.
   173	    /// This operation will track the read range for conflict detection in SSI mode.
   174	    ///
   175	    /// ## Arguments
   176	    /// - `range`: the range of keys to scan
   177	    ///
   178	    /// ## Returns
   179	    /// - `Result<DbIterator, SlateDBError>`: An iterator with the results of the scan
   180	    pub async fn scan<K, T>(&self, range: T) -> Result<DbIterator, crate::Error>
   181	    where
   182	        K: AsRef<[u8]> + Send,
   183	        T: RangeBounds<K> + Send,
   184	    {
   185	        self.scan_with_options(range, &ScanOptions::default()).await
   186	    }
   187	
   188	    /// Scan a range of keys with the provided options.
   189	    /// This operation will track the read range for conflict detection in SSI mode.
   190	    ///
   191	    /// ## Arguments
   192	    /// - `range`: the range of keys to scan
   193	    /// - `options`: the scan options to use
   194	    ///
   195	    /// ## Returns
   196	    /// - `Result<DbIterator, SlateDBError>`: An iterator with the results of the scan
   197	    pub async fn scan_with_options<K, T>(
   198	        &self,
   199	        range: T,
   200	        options: &ScanOptions,
   201	    ) -> Result<DbIterator, crate::Error>
   202	    where
   203	        K: AsRef<[u8]> + Send,
   204	        T: RangeBounds<K> + Send,
   205	    {
   206	        // TODO: this range conversion logic can be extract to an util
   207	        let start = range
   208	            .start_bound()
   209	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   210	        let end = range
   211	            .end_bound()
   212	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   213	        let range = (start, end);
   214	
   215	        // Track read range for SSI conflict detection if needed
   216	        let range_tracker = if self.isolation_level == IsolationLevel::SerializableSnapshot {
   217	            let tracker = Arc::new(DbIteratorRangeTracker::new());
   218	            self.range_trackers.lock().push(tracker.clone());
   219	            Some(tracker)
   220	        } else {
   221	            None
   222	        };
   223	
   224	        self.db_inner.check_closed()?;
   225	        let db_state = self.db_inner.state.read().view();
   226	
   227	        // Clone the WriteBatch for the scan to ensure that the scan within a transaction
   228	        // sees a consistent view of the current writes.
   229	        let write_batch_cloned = self.write_batch.read().clone();
   230	
   231	        // For now, delegate to the underlying reader
   232	        self.db_inner
   233	            .reader
   234	            .scan_with_options(
   235	                BytesRange::from(range),
   236	                options,
   237	                &db_state,
   238	                Some(write_batch_cloned),
   239	                Some(self.started_seq),
   240	                range_tracker,
   241	            )
   242	            .await
   243	            .map_err(Into::into)
   244	    }

   301	    /// Put a key-value pair into the transaction with custom options.

   303	    ///

   306	    /// - `value`: the value to write
   307	    /// - `options`: the put options to use
   308	    ///
   309	    /// ## Errors
   310	    /// - It's not really possible to have error here, since the write operation is
   311	    ///   buffered in the write batch.
   312	    pub fn put_with_options<K, V>(
   313	        &self,
   314	        key: K,
   315	        value: V,
   316	        options: &PutOptions,
   317	    ) -> Result<(), crate::Error>
   318	    where

   320	        V: AsRef<[u8]>,
   321	    {
   322	        self.write_batch
   323	            .write()
   324	            .put_with_options(key, value, options);
   325	        Ok(())
   326	    }
   327	
   328	    /// Mark keys as read for conflict detection.
   329	    ///
   330	    /// This method explicitly tracks read operations for conflict detection. When keys are
   331	    /// marked as read, the transaction will detect conflicts if another transaction modifies
   332	    /// any of those keys after this transaction started, regardless of the isolation level.
   333	    ///
   334	    /// This allows for selective read-write conflict detection even in Snapshot Isolation mode,
   335	    /// where reads are not automatically tracked (unlike `get()` which only tracks reads in SSI
   336	    /// mode).
   337	    ///
   338	    /// ## Arguments
   339	    /// - `keys`: an iterator of keys to mark as read
   340	    ///
   341	    /// ## Examples
   342	    /// ```rust
   343	    /// # async fn example() -> Result<(), slatedb::Error> {
   344	    /// # use std::sync::Arc;
   345	    /// # use slatedb::object_store::memory::InMemory;
   346	    /// use slatedb::{Db, IsolationLevel};
   347	    ///
   348	    /// # let object_store = Arc::new(InMemory::new());
   349	    /// # let db = Db::open("test_path", object_store).await?;
   350	    /// let txn = db.begin(IsolationLevel::Snapshot).await?;
   351	    /// txn.mark_read([b"key1", b"key2", b"key3"])?;
   352	    /// # Ok(())
   353	    /// # }
   354	    /// ```
   355	    pub fn mark_read<K, I>(&self, keys: I) -> Result<(), crate::Error>
   356	    where
   357	        K: AsRef<[u8]>,
   358	        I: IntoIterator<Item = K>,
   359	    {
   360	        // Always track reads when explicitly marked, regardless of isolation level.
   361	        // The current conflict checking logic always checks the read_keys set
   362	        // even in SI mode. The only difference between SI and SSI is whether
   363	        // the read keys are tracked in the read set or not.
   364	
   365	        let read_keys = keys.into_iter().map(|k| Bytes::copy_from_slice(k.as_ref()));
   366	        self.txn_manager.track_read_keys(&self.txn_id, read_keys);
   367	        Ok(())
   368	    }
   369	
   370	    /// Mark written keys as untracked for conflict detection.
   371	    ///
   372	    /// Keys marked with this method are still written atomically with the rest of the
   373	    /// transaction, but are excluded from transaction conflict detection on commit for
   374	    /// both this transaction and other transactions.
   375	    ///
   376	    /// This means:
   377	    /// - If another transaction reads a key written with an `unmark_write` by this transaction, that key
   378	    ///   will not cause a read-write conflict.
   379	    /// - If another transaction writes a key written with an `unmark_write` by this transaction, that key
   380	    ///   will not cause a write-write conflict.
   381	    ///
   382	    /// You may call `unmark_write` either before or after writing a key in the transaction.
   383	    /// Once a key is unmarked, it cannot be marked again within the same transaction and
   384	    /// remains unmarked for the duration of this transaction, even if `put`, `merge`, or
   385	    /// `delete` is called on the same key later in the transaction.
   386	    ///
   387	    /// ## Arguments
   388	    /// - `keys`: an iterator of keys to exclude from write conflict tracking
   389	    ///
   390	    /// ## Examples
   391	    /// ```rust
   392	    /// # async fn example() -> Result<(), slatedb::Error> {
   393	    /// # use std::sync::Arc;
   394	    /// # use slatedb::object_store::memory::InMemory;
   395	    /// use slatedb::{Db, IsolationLevel};
   396	    ///
   397	    /// # let object_store = Arc::new(InMemory::new());
   398	    /// # let db = Db::open("test_path", object_store).await?;
   399	    /// let txn = db.begin(IsolationLevel::Snapshot).await?;
   400	    /// txn.put(b"counter", b"1")?;
   401	    /// txn.unmark_write([b"counter"])?;
   402	    /// txn.put(b"counter", b"2")?;
   403	    /// txn.commit().await?;
   404	    /// # Ok(())
   405	    /// # }
   406	    /// ```
   407	    pub fn unmark_write<K, I>(&self, keys: I) -> Result<(), crate::Error>
   408	    where
   409	        K: AsRef<[u8]>,
   410	        I: IntoIterator<Item = K>,
   411	    {
   412	        let mut untracked_keys = self.untracked_write_keys.write();
   413	        untracked_keys.extend(keys.into_iter().map(|k| Bytes::copy_from_slice(k.as_ref())));
   414	        Ok(())
   415	    }
   416	
   417	    /// Merge a key-value pair into the transaction.
   418	    pub fn merge<K, V>(&self, key: K, value: V) -> Result<(), crate::Error>
   419	    where
   420	        K: AsRef<[u8]>,
   421	        V: AsRef<[u8]>,
   422	    {
   423	        self.merge_with_options(key, value, &MergeOptions::default())
   424	    }
   425	
   426	    /// Merge a key-value pair into the transaction with custom options.
   427	    pub fn merge_with_options<K, V>(
   428	        &self,
   429	        key: K,
   430	        value: V,
   431	        options: &MergeOptions,
   432	    ) -> Result<(), crate::Error>
   433	    where
   434	        K: AsRef<[u8]>,
   435	        V: AsRef<[u8]>,
   436	    {
   437	        self.write_batch
   438	            .write()
   439	            .merge_with_options(key, value, options);
   440	        Ok(())
   441	    }
   442	
   443	    /// Delete a key from the transaction.
   444	    /// The delete will be buffered in the transaction's write batch until commit.
   445	    ///
   446	    /// ## Arguments
   447	    /// - `key`: the key to delete
   448	    ///
   449	    /// ## Errors
   450	    /// - It's not really possible to have error here, since the delet<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you.     92	        let mut b = BytesMut::from(a.as_ref());

    98	        nonempty_bytes(size).prop_flat_map(|a| {
    99	            let a_extended = extend_bytes(&a, u8::MIN);
   100	            prop_oneof![
   101	                Just(BytesRange::new(Included(a.clone()), Included(a.clone()))),
   102	                Just(BytesRange::new(
   103	                    Included(a.clone()),

   110	
   111	    fn min_and_max(a: Bytes, b: Bytes) -> (Bytes, Bytes) {
   112	        if a < b {
   113	            (a, b)
   114	        } else {
   115	            (b, a)
   116	        }
   117	    }
   118	
   119	    fn nonempty_range_filter(tuple: (Bytes, Bytes)) -> Option<(Bytes, Bytes)> {
   120	        let (a, b) = tuple;
   121	        if a == b {
   122	            None
   123	        } else {
   124	            let (start, end) = min_and_max(a, b);
   125	            if bytes_range::is_prefix_increment(&start, &end) {
   126	                None
   127	            } else {
   128	                Some((start, end))
   129	            }
   130	        }
   131	    }
   132	
   133	    pub(crate) fn empty_range(size: usize) -> impl Strategy<Value = BytesRange> {
   134	        nonempty_bytes(size).prop_flat_map(|a| {
   135	            prop_oneof![
   136	                Just(BytesRange::new(Excluded(a.clone()), Excluded(a.clone()))),
   137	                Just(BytesRange::new(Included(a.clone()), Excluded(a.clone()))),
   138	                Just(BytesRange::new(Excluded(a.clone()), Included(a))),
   139	            ]
   140	        })
   141	    }
   142	
   143	    pub(crate) fn nonempty_range(size: usize) -> impl Strategy<Value = BytesRange> {
   144	        prop_oneof![
   145	            Just(BytesRange::new(Unbounded, Unbounded)),
   146	            arbitrary_single_point_bounded_range(size),
   147	            nonempty_partial_bounded_range(size),
   148	            nonempty_bounded_range(size),
   149	        ]
   150	    }
   151	
   152	    pub(crate) fn nonempty_intersecting_ranges(
   153	        size: usize,
   154	    ) -> impl Strategy<Value = (BytesRange, BytesRange)> {
   155	        (rng(), nonempty_range(size)).prop_flat_map(|(mut rng, range1)| {
   156	            let start = sample::bytes_in_range(&mut rng, &range1);
   157	            let end_range = BytesRange::new(Included(start.clone()), Unbounded);
   158	            let end = sample::bytes_in_range(&mut rng, &end_range);
   159	            prop_oneof![
   160	                (
   161	                    Just(range1.clone()),
   162	                    Just(BytesRange::new(
   163	                        Included(start.clone()),
   164	                        Included(end.clone())
   165	                    ))
   166	                ),
   167	                (
   168	                    Just(range1.clone()),
   169	                    Just(BytesRange::new(Unbounded, Included(end)))
   170	                ),
   171	                (
   172	                    Just(range1.clone()),
   173	                    Just(BytesRange::new(Included(start), Unbounded))
   174	                ),
   175	                (
   176	                    Just(range1.clone()),
   177	                    Just(BytesRange::new(Unbounded, Unbounded))
   178	                ),
   179	            ]
   180	        })
   181	    }
   182	}

   189	    pub(crate) fn new_test_rng(seed: Option<[u8; 32]>) -> TestRng {
   190	        let seed = seed.unwrap_or_else(|| {
   191	            let mut thread_rng = rand::rng();
   192	            let random_bytes: [u8; 32] = thread_rng.random();
   193	            random_bytes
   194	        });
   195	        TestRng::from_seed(RngAlgorithm::ChaCha, &seed)
   196	    }

   198	
   199	/// Sometimes it is more convenient to generate individual values. This can be
   200	/// useful when we need a sample value which is derived from arbitrary inputs
   201	/// or when the generation of the sample is expensive. For example, it
   202	/// would be too expensive to treat a table of key-value pairs as an arbitrary
   203	/// input into a property test. Instead, we might generate a single arbitrary
   204	/// table sample and use it to seed the database. Then we can run property tests
   205	/// against the database. We nevertheless want the sample table to be deterministically
   206	/// generated so that the test failure can be easily reproduced.
   207	#[cfg(test)]
   208	pub(crate) mod sample {
   209	    use crate::bytes_range::BytesRange;
   210	    use crate::{bytes_range, test_utils};
   211	    use bytes::{BufMut, Bytes, BytesMut};
   212	    use proptest::test_runner::TestRng;
   213	    use rand::distr::uniform::SampleRange;
   214	    use rand::prelude::SliceRandom;
   215	    use rand::Rng;
   216	    use std::cmp::max;
   217	    use std::collections::BTreeMap;
   218	    use std::ops::Bound::{Excluded, Included, Unbounded};
   219	    use std::ops::{Bound, RangeBounds};
   220	
   221	    pub(crate) fn bytes<T: SampleRange<usize>>(rng: &mut TestRng, len_range: T) -> Bytes {
   222	        let len = rng.random_range(len_range);
   223	        let mut v: Vec<u8> = Vec::with_capacity(len);
   224	        for _ in 0..len {
   225	            v.push(rng.random());
   226	        }
   227	        v.into()
   228	    }
   229	
   230	    pub(crate) fn record(rng: &mut TestRng, max_bytes_len: usize) -> (Bytes, Bytes) {
   231	        let key = bytes(rng, 1..max_bytes_len);
   232	        let value = bytes(rng, 0..max_bytes_len);
   233	        (key, value)
   234	    }
   235	
   236	    pub(crate) fn table(
   237	        rng: &mut TestRng,
   238	        num_records: usize,
   239	        max_bytes_len: usize,
   240	    ) -> BTreeMap<Bytes, Bytes> {
   241	        let mut table = BTreeMap::new();
   242	        while table.len() < num_records {
   243	            let (key, value) = record(rng, max_bytes_len);
   244	            table.insert(key, value);
   245	        }
   246	        table
   247	    }
   248	
   249	    fn bytes_between(rng: &mut TestRng, start: &Bytes, end: &Bytes) -> Bytes {
   250	        assert_eq!(start.len(), end.len());
   251	        let mut res = BytesMut::new();
   252	        let mut start_bound_satisfied = false;
   253	        let mut end_bound_satisfied = false;
   254	        let min_len = rng.random_range(0..=start.len());
   255	
   256	        for i in 0..start.len() {
   257	            let next_val_lb = if !start_bound_satisfied {
   258	                start[i]
   259	            } else {
   260	                u8::MIN
   261	            };
   262	            let next_val_ub = if !end_bound_satisfied {
   263	                end[i]
   264	            } else {
   265	                u8::MAX
   266	            };
   267	
   268	            let next_val = if next_val_lb == next_val_ub {
   269	                next_val_lb
   270	            } else {
   271	                let next_bound_range_diff = next_val_ub - next_val_lb;
   272	                next_val_lb + (rng.random::<u8>() % next_bound_range_diff)
   273	            };
   274	            res.put_u8(next_val);
   275	
   276	            if next_val > next_val_lb {
   277	                start_bound_satisfied = true;
   278	            }
   279	
   280	            if next_val < next_val_ub {
   281	                end_bound_satisfied = true;
   282	            }
   283	
   284	            if start_bound_satisfied && end_bound_satisfied && res.len() >= min_len {
   285	                break;
   286	            }
   287	        }
   288	
   289	        let res = res.freeze();
   290	        assert!(res >= start && res <= end);
   291	        res
   292	    }
   293	
   294	    fn increment_lex(b: &Bytes) -> Bytes {
   295	        let mut res = BytesMut::from(b.as_ref());
   296	        for i in (0..res.len()).rev() {
   297	            if res[i] < u8::MAX {
   298	                res[i] += 1;
   299	                return res.freeze();
   300	            } else {
   301	                res[i] = u8::MIN;
   302	            }
   303	        }
   304	        panic!("Overflow when incrementing bytes {b:?}")
   305	    }
   306	
   307	    fn decrement_lex(b: &Bytes) -> Bytes {
   308	        let mut res = BytesMut::from(b.as_ref());
   309	        for i in (0..res.len()).rev() {
   310	            if res[i] > u8::MIN {
   311	                res[i] -= 1;
   312	                return res.freeze();
   313	            } else {
   314	                res[i] = u8::MAX;
   315	            }
   316	        }
   317	        panic!("Overflow when decrementing bytes {b:?}")
   318	    }
   319	
   320	    /// Get a random byte array which has [`u8::MIN`] at each index and is
   321	    /// between the min and max bounds (which are assumed to also be arrays
   322	    /// of [`u8::MIN`]).
   323	    fn minvalue_bytes(
   324	        rng: &mut TestRng,
   325	        min_bound: Bound<usize>,
   326	        max_bound: Bound<usize>,
   327	    ) -> Bytes {
   328	        let min_len = match min_bound {
   329	            Unbounded => 0,
   330	            Included(len) => len,
   331	            Excluded(len) => len + 1,
   332	        };
   333	
   334	        let max_len = match max_bound {
   335	            Unbounded => min_len + 10,
   336	            Included(len) => len,
   337	            Excluded(len) => len - 1,
   338	        };
   339	
   340	        let len = rng.random_range(min_len..=max_len);
   341	        Bytes::from(vec![u8::MIN; len])
   342	    }
   343	
   344	    fn bound_len(bound: Bound<&Bytes>) -> usize {
   345	        match bound {
   346	            Unbounded => 0,
   347	            Included(b) | Excluded(b) => b.len(),
   348	        }
   349	    }
   350	
   351	    fn padded_bytes(b: &[u8], value: u8, len: usize) -> Bytes {
   352	        let mut padded = BytesMut::from(b);
   353	        while padded.len() < len {
   354	            padded.put_u8(value);
   355	        }
   356	        padded.freeze()
   357	    }
   358	
   359	    fn inclusive_end_bound(range: &BytesRange, len: usize) -> Bytes {
   360	        match range.end_bound() {
   361	            Unbounded => padded_bytes(&Bytes::new(), u8::MAX, len),
   362	            Included(b) | Excluded(b) => {
   363	                let b = padded_bytes(b, u8::MIN, len);
   364	                decrement_lex(&b)
   365	            }
   366	        }
   367	    }
   368	
   369	    fn inclusive_start_bound(range: &BytesRange, len: usize) -> Bytes {
   370	        match range.start_bound() {
   371	            Unbounded => padded_bytes(&Bytes::new(), u8::MIN, len),
   372	            Included(b) => padded_bytes(b, u8::MIN, len),
   373	            Excluded(b) => {
   374	                let padded = padded_bytes(b, u8::MIN, len);
   375	                if b.len() < len {
   376	                    padded
   377	                } else {
   378	                    increment_lex(&padded)
   379	                }
   380	            }
   381	        }
   382	    }
   383	
   384	    fn can_decrement_without_truncation(bytes: &Bytes) -> bool {
   385	        bytes.iter().any(|b| *b > u8::MIN)
   386	    }
   387	
   388	    pub(crate) fn bytes_in_range(rng: &mut TestRng, range: &BytesRange) -> Bytes {
   389	        assert!(
   390	            range.non_empty(),
   391	            "Cannot choose an arbitrary value from an empty range"
   392	        );
   393	
   394	        if let Some(end) = test_utils::bound_as_option(range.end_bound()) {
   395	            if !can_decrement_without_truncation(end) {
   396	                let min_len = match range.start_bound() {
   397	                    // If start bound is unbounded, minvalue_bytes uses 0 as the length,
   398	                    // and random_range(0 ..) is inclusive. This can lead to an empty length
   399	                    // result, which will trigger a failure in the assertion below (is_empty).
   400	                    // Prevent this by using Excluded(0) as the min len so we get a non-empty
   401	                    // result no matter what.
   402	                    Unbounded => Excluded(0),
   403	                    Included(b) => Included(b.len()),
   404	                    Excluded(b) => Excluded(b.len()),
   405	                };
   406	                let max_len = range.end_bound().map(|b| b.len());
   407	                let result = minvalue_bytes(rng, min_len, max_len);
   408	                assert!(
   409	                    !result.is_empty(),
   410	                    "calculated empty bytes for range {range:?}"
   411	                );
   412	                return result;
   413	            } else if range.start_bound() == Included(end) {
   414	                return end.clone();
   415	            } else {
   416	                let start = test_utils::bound_as_option(range.start_bound())
   417	                    .cloned()
   418	                    .unwrap_or_default();
   419	                if bytes_range::is_prefix_increment(&start, end) {
   420	                    let mut tmp = Vec::new();
   421	                    if matches!(range.start_bound(), Included(_) | Unbounded) {
   422	                        tmp.push(start);
   423	                    }
   424	                    if matches!(range.end_bound(), Included(_)) {
   425	                        tmp.push(end.clone());
   426	                    }
   427	                    tmp.shuffle(rng);
   428	                    return tmp.pop().unwrap();
   429	                }
   430	            }
   431	        }
   432	
   433	        let len = max(bound_len(range.start_bound()), bound_len(range.end_bound())) + 3;
   434	        let start_bound = inclusive_start_bound(range, len);
   435	        let end_bound = inclusive_end_bound(range, len);
   436	        bytes_between(rng, &start_bound, &end_bound)
   437	    }
   438	}

Now let me understand the issue better. The PR description mentions that with PR #1401, users might supply `RangeBounds<Bytes>` that have empty start or ending bounds. The `BytesRange::new` currently throws/panics with such empty bounds. The fix should change `BytesRange` to accept empty bounds.

But wait - we need to think about what "accepting empty bounds" means. An empty byte array `[]` is a valid key - it's the empty key. The current code rejects it because `is_bound_non_empty` returns false for empty byte arrays. But an empty key is a valid key that users might want to use.

However, there's also the question: does allowing empty bounds cause any issues? Let me check the `ComparableRange::non_empty` method:

Looking at `comparable_range.rs` line 265-274:
```rust
pub(crate) fn non_empty(&self) -> bool {
    match (&self.start.inner, &self.end.inner) {
        (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Included(b)) => a <= b,
        (Bound::Included(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => a < b,
        (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Excluded(b)) => a < b,
        (Bound::Excluded(a), Bound::Included(b)) => a < b,
        (Bound::Unbounded, _) => true,
        (_, Bound::Unbounded) => true,
    }
}
```

If both bounds are `Included([])` (empty bytes), then `[] <= []` is true, so the range would be non-empty (it contains the empty key). That seems correct.

If we have `Included([])` and `Excluded([])`, then `[] < []` is false, so the range would be empty. That also seems correct.

So the `ComparableRange::non_empty` handles empty bounds correctly. The only issue is the `is_bound_non_empty` check in `BytesRange::new` that prevents empty bounds from being used at all.

Let me now make the change to remove the assertions that prevent empty bounds:
