     1	use bytes::Bytes;
     2	use serde::Serialize;
     3	use std::ops::Bound::{Excluded, Included, Unbounded};
     4	use std::ops::{Bound, RangeBounds};
     5	
     6	use crate::comparable_range::{ComparableRange, EndBound, StartBound};
     7	
     8	/// Concrete struct representing a range of Bytes. Gets around much of
     9	/// the cumbersome work associated with the generic trait RangeBounds<Bytes>
    10	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq, Ord, PartialOrd, Hash)]
    11	pub(crate) struct BytesRange {
    12	    inner: ComparableRange<Bytes>,
    13	}
    14	
    15	impl Serialize for BytesRange {
    16	    fn serialize<S>(&self, serializer: S) -> Result<S::Ok, S::Error>
    17	    where
    18	        S: serde::Serializer,
    19	    {
    20	        self.inner.serialize(serializer)
    21	    }
    22	}
    23	
    24	#[cfg(test)]
    25	// Checks for the annoying case when we have ("prefix", "prefix\0").
    26	// When both bounds are excluded, the range is empty even though
    27	// "prefix" < "prefix\0".
    28	pub(crate) fn is_prefix_increment(prefix: &[u8], b: &[u8]) -> bool {
    29	    if !b.starts_with(prefix.as_ref()) {
    30	        return false;
    31	    }
    32	
    33	    b[prefix.len()..] == [u8::MIN]
    34	}
    35	
    36	impl RangeBounds<Bytes> for BytesRange {
    37	    fn start_bound(&self) -> Bound<&Bytes> {
    38	        self.inner.start_bound()
    39	    }
    40	
    41	    fn end_bound(&self) -> Bound<&Bytes> {
    42	        self.inner.end_bound()
    43	    }
    44	}
    45	
    46	impl BytesRange {
    47	    pub(crate) fn new(start_bound: Bound<Bytes>, end_bound: Bound<Bytes>) -> Self {
    48	        let inner = ComparableRange::new(start_bound, end_bound);
    49	        assert!(inner.non_empty(), "Range must be non-empty");
    50	        Self { inner }
    51	    }
    52	
    53	    pub(crate) fn new_empty() -> Self {
    54	        Self {
    55	            inner: ComparableRange::new(
    56	                Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(&[0_u8])),
    57	                Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(&[0_u8])),
    58	            ),
    59	        }
    60	    }
    61	
    62	    pub(crate) fn from<T: RangeBounds<Bytes>>(range: T) -> Self {
    63	        Self::new(range.start_bound().cloned(), range.end_bound().cloned())
    64	    }
    65	
    66	    pub(crate) fn from_slice<'a, T>(range: T) -> Self
    67	    where
    68	        T: RangeBounds<&'a [u8]>,
    69	    {
    70	        Self::new(
    71	            range.start_bound().map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b)),
    72	            range.end_bound().map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b)),
    73	        )
    74	    }
    75	
    76	    /// Build a half-open range `[prefix, prefix+1)` covering all keys that start with
    77	    /// `prefix`.
    78	    ///
    79	    /// - Empty prefix returns `(..)` so callers can scan the entire keyspace.
    80	    /// - If the prefix is all `0xff`, the end bound is unbounded rather than overflowing.
    81	    pub(crate) fn from_prefix(prefix: &[u8]) -> Self {
    82	        if prefix.is_empty() {
    83	            return Self::new(Unbounded, Unbounded);
    84	        }
    85	
    86	        let start = Bytes::copy_from_slice(prefix);
    87	        let end = Self::increment_prefix(prefix)
    88	            .map(Excluded)
    89	            .unwrap_or(Unbounded);
    90	        Self::new(Included(start), end)
    91	    }
    92	
    93	    /// Compute the smallest byte string that is lexicographically greater than any key
    94	    /// starting with `prefix`. Returns `None` when `prefix` is all `0xff`.
    95	    fn increment_prefix(prefix: &[u8]) -> Option<Bytes> {
    96	        let mut upper_bound = prefix.to_vec();
    97	
    98	        for i in (0..upper_bound.len()).rev() {
    99	            if upper_bound[i] != u8::MAX {
   100	                upper_bound[i] += 1;
   101	                upper_bound.truncate(i + 1);
   102	                return Some(Bytes::from(upper_bound));
   103	            }
   104	        }
   105	
   106	        None
   107	    }
   108	
   109	    #[cfg(test)]
   110	    pub(crate) fn from_ref<K, T>(range: T) -> Self
   111	    where
   112	        K: AsRef<[u8]>,
   113	        T: RangeBounds<K>,
   114	    {
   115	        let start = range
   116	            .start_bound()
   117	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   118	        let end = range
   119	            .end_bound()
   120	            .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
   121	        Self::new(start, end)
   122	    }
   123	
   124	    pub(crate) fn intersect(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Self> {
   125	        self.inner
   126	            .intersect(&other.inner)
   127	            .map(|inner| Self { inner })
   128	    }
   129	
   130	    pub(crate) fn is_start_bound_included_or_unbounded(&self) -> bool {
   131	        !matches!(self.start_bound(), Excluded(_))
   132	    }
   133	
   134	    #[cfg(test)]
   135	    pub(crate) fn non_empty(&self) -> bool {
   136	        self.inner.non_empty()
   137	    }
   138	
   139	    #[cfg(test)]
   140	    pub(crate) fn empty(&self) -> bool {
   141	        !self.inner.non_empty()
   142	    }
   143	
   144	    pub(crate) fn comparable_start_bound(&self) -> StartBound<&Bytes> {
   145	        self.inner.comparable_start_bound()
   146	    }
   147	
   148	    pub(crate) fn comparable_end_bound(&self) -> EndBound<&Bytes> {
   149	        self.inner.comparable_end_bound()
   150	    }
   151	
   152	    pub(crate) fn as_point(&self) -> Option<&Bytes> {
   153	        match (self.start_bound(), self.end_bound()) {
   154	            (Bound::Included(start), Bound::Included(end)) if start == end => Some(start),
   155	            _ => None,
   156	        }
   157	    }
   158	}

   238	            suffix in arbitrary::bytes(8)
   239	        )| {
   240	            let range = BytesRange::from_prefix(&prefix);
   241	
   242	            // Any key starting with the prefix should be contained.
   243	            let mut prefixed = prefix.to_vec();
   244	            prefixed.extend_from_slice(&suffix);
   245	            let prefixed = Bytes::from(prefixed);
   246	            prop_assert!(range.contains(&prefixed));

   251	            let non_prefixed = Bytes::from(non_prefixed);
   252	            prop_assert!(!range.contains(&non_prefixed));

2026-05-31 08:51:33,208 - INFO - swea-agent-slatedb__slatedb-1461 - 💭 THOUGHT
All tests pass across the workspace. Now let me think about edge cases.

The change I made was to remove the `is_bound_non_empty` check from `BytesRange::new`. This means:
1. Empty byte arrays `[]` can now be used as bounds
2. The remaining assertion `assert!(inner.non_empty(), "Range must be non-empty")` still ensures the range itself is non-empty

Let me verify some edge cases:

1. **`Included([])` to `Included([])`**: This is a valid non-empty range containing only the empty key. `[] <= []` is true. ✅
2. **`Included([])` to `Excluded([])`**: This is empty because `[] < []` is false. The assertion would catch this. ✅
3. **`Excluded([])` to `Included([])`**: This is empty because `[] < []` is false. The assertion would catch this. ✅
4. **`Excluded([])` to `Excluded([])`**: This is empty because `[] < []` is false. The assertion would catch this. ✅
5. **`Included([])` to `Unbounded`**: Non-empty (contains all keys >= empty). ✅
6. **`Unbounded` to `Included([])`**: Non-empty (contains all keys <= empty, which is just the empty key). ✅
7. **`Included([])` to `Included([0])`**: Non-empty. `[] <= [0]` is true. ✅

These all seem correct. The key insight is that an empty byte array `[]` is a valid key, and there's no reason to reject it as a bound. The only thing that should be rejected is when the range itself is empty (start > end, or excluded bounds where start == end).

Let me also verify that the `new_empty` method still works correctly. It creates a range with `Excluded([0])` for both start and end, which is empty because `[0] < [0]` is false. This is fine.

Let me also think about the `from` method which is the main entry point for users. In `db_snapshot.rs` and `db_transaction.rs`, the code does:

```rust
let start = range
    .start_bound()
    .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
let end = range
    .end_bound()
    .map(|b| Bytes::copy_from_slice(b.as_ref()));
let range = (start, end);
// ...
BytesRange::from(range)
```

This converts a `RangeBounds<K>` to `(Bound<Bytes>, Bound<Bytes>)` and then calls `BytesRange::from` which calls `BytesRange::new`. If the user provides an empty key like `""`, this will now work correctly.

But wait, there's a subtlety: when `range.start_bound()` returns `Included("")` and `range.end_bound()` returns `Included("")`, the `BytesRange::new` will create a non-empty range containing just the empty key. That's correct behavior.

When `range.start_bound()` returns `Included("")` and `range.end_bound()` returns `Excluded("")`, the `BytesRange::new` will panic with "Range must be non-empty". But this is correct - a range that excludes its only element is indeed empty.

I think the change is complete and correct. Let me also quickly check if there are any other places that might have similar checks for empty bounds:

    10	/// A half-open or closed byte-key range used by scan APIs.
    11	#[derive(Clone, Debug, Default, uniffi::Record)]
    12	pub struct KeyRange {
    13	    /// Inclusive or exclusive lower bound. `None` means unbounded.
    14	    pub start: Option<Vec<u8>>,
    15	    /// Whether `start` is inclusive when present.
    16	    pub start_inclusive: bool,
    17	    /// Inclusive or exclusive upper bound. `None` means unbounded.
    18	    pub end: Option<Vec<u8>>,
    19	    /// Whether `end` is inclusive when present.
    20	    pub end_inclusive: bool,
    21	}
    22

    24	    pub(crate) fn into_bounds(self) -> Result<KeyBounds, SlateDbError> {
    25	        if self.start.as_ref().is_some_and(|start| start.is_empty()) {
    26	            return Err(SlateDbError::EmptyRangeStart);
    27	        }
    28	        if self.end.as_ref().is_some_and(|end| end.is_empty()) {
    29	            return Err(SlateDbError::EmptyRangeEnd);
    30	        }

    34	                std::cmp::Ordering::Greater => {
    35	                    return Err(SlateDbError::RangeStartGreaterThanEnd);
    36	                }

    38	                    return Err(SlateDbError::EmptyRange);
    39	                }

    41	            }
    42	        }

1. `db_snapshot.rs:137` - `BytesRange::from(range)` where `range` is `(Bound<Bytes>, Bound<Bytes>)` tuple
2. `db_transaction.rs:235` - `BytesRange::from(range)` where `range` is `(Bound<Bytes>, Bound<Bytes>)` tuple
3. `db.rs:1012` - `BytesRange::from(range)` 

These are the main entry points where a user's `RangeBounds<K>` gets converted to `BytesRange`. With my change, empty bounds (empty byte arrays) will no longer cause a panic.

Let me also verify that the `new_empty` method still creates a valid empty range. The `new_empty` method uses `Excluded(Bytes::copy_from_slice(&[0_u8]))` for both start and end, which creates an empty range because `[0] < [0]` is false. This is fine.

But wait, I need to check: does the `new_empty` method now need to use empty bytes? Actually no, `new_empty` is a special method to create an explicitly empty range. It uses `[0_u8]` as a sentinel value. That's fine and doesn't need to change.

Now, there's one more thing to consider. The PR description says:

> With https://github.com/slatedb/slatedb/pull/1401 users might supply `RangeBounds<Bytes>` that have empty start or ending bounds (an empty bytes array []). This currently throws with the underlying `BytesRange`. The two options seem:
> - Document the behavior correctly.
> - Change the underlying `BytesRange` to except empty bounds.

The decision was to change `BytesRange` to accept empty bounds. My change does exactly that - it removes the two assertions that checked for non-empty bounds, while keeping the assertion that the range itself is non-empty.
